<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sami_shamanic_drum.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Noaidi" title="Noaidi">Sami shamanic drum</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Arktikum_Science_Museum" title="Arktikum Science Museum">Arktikum Science Museum</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Rovaniemi" title="Rovaniemi">Rovaniemi</a>, Finland</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Shamanism_in_Europe" title="Shamanism in Europe">Shamanism in Europe</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Noaidi" title="Noaidi">Noaidi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sami_shamanism" title="Sami shamanism">Sami shamanism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Finnish_mythology" title="Finnish mythology">Finnish mythology</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_mythology" title="Hungarian mythology">Hungarian mythology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shamanistic_remnants_in_Hungarian_folklore" title="Shamanistic remnants in Hungarian folklore">Shamanistic remnants in Hungarian folklore</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magic_in_the_Greco-Roman_world" title="Magic in the Greco-Roman world">Magic in the Greco-Roman world</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_witchcraft" title="European witchcraft">European witchcraft</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astuvansalmi" title="Astuvansalmi">Astuvansalmi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Astuvansalmi_rock_paintings" title="Astuvansalmi rock paintings">Astuvansalmi rock paintings</a></div>
<p>Some of the prehistoric peoples who once lived in Siberia have dispersed and migrated into other regions, bringing aspects of their cultures with them. For example, many Uralic peoples live now outside Siberia, however the original location of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Uralic_language" title="Proto-Uralic language">Proto-Uralic</a> peoples (and its extent) is debated. Combined <a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">phytogeographical</a> and linguistic considerations (distribution of various tree species and the presence of their names in various Uralic languages) suggest that this area was north of Central <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> and on lower and middle parts of <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ancloc_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-ancloc-158">[158]</a></sup> The ancestors of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">Hungarian people</a> or Magyars have wandered from their ancestral proto-Uralic area to the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Basin" title="Pannonian Basin">Pannonian Basin</a>. Shamanism has played an important role in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mythology_of_the_Turkic_and_Mongolian_peoples" title="Mythology of the Turkic and Mongolian peoples">Turko-Mongol mythology</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tengriism" title="Tengriism">Tengriism</a> - the major ancient belief among <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a>, Mongol and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magyars" title="Magyars">Magyars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> - incorporates elements of shamanism. Shamanism is no more a living practice among Hungarians, but remnants have been reserved as fragments of folklore, in folktales, customs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some historians of the Late Middle Ages and Early Modern period have argued that traces of shamanistic traditions can be seen in the popular folk belief of this period. Most prominent among these was the Italian <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ginzburg" title="Carlo Ginzburg">Carlo Ginzburg</a>, who claimed shamanistic elements in the <i><a href="/wiki/Benandanti" title="Benandanti">benandanti</a></i> custom of 16th century Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> the Hungarian <a href="/wiki/%C3%89va_P%C3%B3cs" title="Éva Pócs">Éva Pócs</a>, who identified them in the <i><a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1ltos" title="Táltos">táltos</a></i> tradition of Hungary,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> and the Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Claude_Lecouteux" title="Claude Lecouteux">Claude Lecouteux</a>, who has argued that Medieval traditions regarding the soul are based on earlier shamanic ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Ginzburg in particular has argued that some of these traditions influenced the conception of <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a> in Christendom, in particular ideas regarding the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Witches%27_sabbath" title="Witches' sabbath">witches' sabbath</a>, leading to the events of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Witch_trials_in_the_Early_Modern_period" title="Witch trials in the Early Modern period">witch trials in the Early Modern period</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Some of these Italian traditions survived into the 20th and early 21st centuries, allowing Italian-American sociologist Sabina Magliocco to make a brief study of them (2009).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Circumpolar_shamanism">Circumpolar shamanism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Circumpolar shamanism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inuit_and_Yupik_cultures">Inuit and Yupik cultures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Inuit and Yupik cultures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="924" data-file-width="550" height="370" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg/220px-Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg/330px-Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg/440px-Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yupik_shaman_Nushagak.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Yup'ik shaman exorcising evil spirits from a sick boy, <a href="/wiki/Nushagak,_Alaska" title="Nushagak, Alaska">Nushagak, Alaska</a>, 1890s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Nushagak, located on <a href="/wiki/Nushagak_Bay" title="Nushagak Bay">Nushagak Bay</a> of the Bering Sea in southwest <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, is part of the territory of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik">Yup'ik</a>, speakers of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik language</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shamanism_among_Eskimo_peoples" title="Shamanism among Eskimo peoples">Shamanism among Eskimo peoples</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eskimo" title="Eskimo">Eskimo</a> groups inhabit a huge area stretching from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Siberia" title="Eastern Siberia">Eastern Siberia</a> through Alaska and Northern Canada (including <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Peninsula" title="Labrador Peninsula">Labrador Peninsula</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>. Shamanistic practice and beliefs have been recorded at several parts of this vast area crosscutting continental borders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mer-BecHalfHid_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Mer-BecHalfHid-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gab-KarEszk_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gab-KarEszk-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KleiSon-Esk_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-KleiSon-Esk-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet"><img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">rendering support</a>, you may see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>When speaking of "shamanism" in various Eskimo groups, we must remember that (as mentioned above) the term "shamanism" can cover certain characteristics of <i>various</i> different cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cogmap_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-cogmap-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="#Mediator">Mediation</a> is regarded often as an important aspect of shamanism in general.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-med_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-med-167">[167]</a></sup> Also in most Eskimo groups, the role of mediator is known well:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-menmed_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-menmed-168">[168]</a></sup> the person filling it in is actually believed to be able to contact the beings who populate the belief system. Term "shaman" is used in several English-language publications also in relation to Eskimos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mer-BecHalfHid_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-Mer-BecHalfHid-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KleiSon-Esk_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-KleiSon-Esk-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Also the <i>alignalghi</i> (<small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Inuktitut" title="Help:IPA for Inuktitut">[aˈliɣnalʁi]</a></span>) of the Asian Eskimos is translated as "shaman" in the Russian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> and English<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-menmed_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-menmed-168">[168]</a></sup> literature.</p>
<p>The belief system assumes specific links between the living people, the souls of hunted animals, and those of dead people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a> concepts of several groups are specific examples of <a href="/wiki/Soul_dualism" title="Soul dualism">soul dualism</a> (showing variability in details in the various cultures).</p>
<p>Unlike the majority of shamanisms the careers of most Eskimo shamans lack the motivation of <i>force</i>: becoming a shaman is usually a result of deliberate consideration, not a necessity forced by the spirits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-failed-shaman_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-failed-shaman-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity.2C_with_similarities">Diversity, with similarities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Diversity, with similarities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Another possible concern: do the belief systems of various Eskimo groups have such common features at all, that would justify any mentioning them together? There was no political structure above the groups, their languages were relative, but differed more or less, often forming <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Language_continuum" title="Language continuum">language continuums</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-complink_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-complink-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are similarities in the cultures of the Eskimo groups<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-padlgreen_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-padlgreen-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mau-Mor_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mau-Mor-178">[178]</a></sup> together with diversity, far from homogeneity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Russian linguist Menovshikov (Меновщиков), an expert of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Yupik_language" title="Siberian Yupik language">Siberian Yupik</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sireniki_Eskimo_language" title="Sireniki Eskimo language">Sireniki Eskimo languages</a> (while admitting that he is not a specialist in ethnology)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> mentions, that the shamanistic seances of those <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Yupik" title="Siberian Yupik">Siberian Yupik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sirenik_Eskimos" title="Sirenik Eskimos">Sireniki</a> groups he has seen have many similarities to those of Greenland Inuit groups described by <a href="/wiki/Fridtjof_Nansen" title="Fridtjof Nansen">Fridtjof Nansen</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> although a large distance separates Siberia and Greenland. There may be certain similarities also in Asiatic groups with North American ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Also the usage of a specific shaman's language is documented among several Eskimo groups, used mostly for talking to spirits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Also the Ungazighmiit (belonging to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Yupik" title="Siberian Yupik">Siberian Yupiks</a>) had a special <a href="/wiki/Allegory" title="Allegory">allegoric</a> usage of some expressions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>The local cultures showed great diversity. The myths concerning the role of shaman had several variants, and also the name of their protagonists varied from culture to culture. For example, a mythological figure, usually referred to in the literature by the collective term <a href="/wiki/Sedna_(mythology)" title="Sedna (mythology)">Sea Woman</a>, has factually many local names: Nerrivik "meat dish" among Polar Inuit, Nuliayuk "lubricous" among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netsilingmiut" title="Netsilingmiut">Netsilingmiut</a>, Sedna "the nether one" among Baffin Land Inuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Also the soul conceptions, e.g. the details of the <a href="/wiki/Soul_dualism" title="Soul dualism">soul dualism</a> showed great variability, ranging from guardianship to a kind of <a href="/wiki/Reincarnation" title="Reincarnation">reincarnation</a>. Conceptions of spirits or other beings had also many variants (see e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Tupilaq" title="Tupilaq">tupilaq</a> concept).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Medicine_man" title="Medicine man">Medicine man</a> and <a href="/wiki/Native_American_religion" title="Native American religion">Native American religion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:White_indian_conjuror.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="629" data-file-width="800" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/White_indian_conjuror.jpg/220px-White_indian_conjuror.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/White_indian_conjuror.jpg/330px-White_indian_conjuror.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/White_indian_conjuror.jpg/440px-White_indian_conjuror.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:White_indian_conjuror.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a> "conjuror" in a 1590 engraving</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1462" data-file-width="1116" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg/220px-Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg/330px-Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg/440px-Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hamatsa_shaman2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hamatsa" title="Hamatsa">Hamatsa</a> ritualist, 1914</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> cultures have diverse religious beliefs and there was never one universal Native American religion or spiritual system. Although many Native American cultures have traditional healers, ritualists, singers, <a href="/wiki/Mysticism" title="Mysticism">mystics</a>, lore-keepers and <a href="/wiki/Medicine_man" title="Medicine man">Medicine people</a>, none of them ever used, or use, the term "shaman" to describe these religious leaders. Rather, like other indigenous cultures the world over, their spiritual functionaries are described by words in their own languages, and in many cases are not taught to outsiders.</p>
<p>Many of these indigenous religions have been grossly misrepresented by outside observers and anthropologists, even to the extent of superficial or seriously mistaken anthropological accounts being taken as more authentic than the accounts of actual members of the cultures and religions in question. Often these accounts suffer from "<a href="/wiki/Noble_savage" title="Noble savage">Noble Savage</a>"-type romanticism and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>. Some contribute to the fallacy that Native American cultures and religions are something that only existed in the past, and which can be mined for data despite the opinions of Native communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Not all Indigenous communities have roles for specific individuals who mediate with the spirit world on behalf of the community. Among those that do have this sort of religious structure, spiritual methods and beliefs may have some commonalities, though many of these commonalities are due to some nations being closely related, from the same region, or through post-Colonial governmental policies leading to the combining of formerly independent nations on reservations. This can sometimes lead to the impression that there is more unity among belief systems than there was in antiquity.</p>
<p>With the arrival of European settlers and colonial administration, the practice of Native American traditional beliefs was discouraged and Christianity was imposed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> upon the indigenous people. In most communities, the traditions were not completely eradicated, but rather went underground, and were practiced secretly until the prohibitive laws were repealed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>Up until and during the last hundred years, thousands of Native American and <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> children from many different communities were sent into the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Indian_residential_school_system" title="Canadian Indian residential school system">Canadian Indian residential school system</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_boarding_school" title="Indian boarding school">Indian boarding schools</a> in an effort to destroy tribal languages, cultures and beliefs. The <a href="/wiki/Trail_of_Tears" title="Trail of Tears">Trail of Tears</a>, in the US, forced Native Americans to relocate from their traditional homes. Canadian laws enacted in 1982, and henceforth, have attempted to reverse previous attempts at extinguishing Native culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Mesoamerica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

</table>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Maya">Maya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Maya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maya_priesthood" title="Maya priesthood">Maya priesthood</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mayan_astrology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mayan astrology (page does not exist)">Mayan astrology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maya_religion" title="Maya religion">Maya religion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mayan_priest_performing_healing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="346" data-file-width="250" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mayan_priest_performing_healing.jpg/220px-Mayan_priest_performing_healing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/30/Mayan_priest_performing_healing.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mayan_priest_performing_healing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Maya_priesthood" title="Maya priesthood">Maya priest</a> performing a healing ritual at <a href="/wiki/Tikal" title="Tikal">Tikal</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Maya people of Guatemala, Belize, and southern Mexico practice astrology and a form of divination known as "the blood speaking", in which the spiritual worker is guided in divination and healing by pulses in the veins of his arms and legs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Aztec">Aztec</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Aztec">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec_astrology" title="Aztec astrology">Aztec astrology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aztec_religion" title="Aztec religion">Aztec religion</a></div>
<p>In contemporary <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a>, there is a spiritual practice known as <i>cualli ohtli</i> – the "good path" followed during dreaming by "friends of the night" to <a href="/wiki/Tlalocan" title="Tlalocan"><i>Tlalocán</i></a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man,_1955.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="731" data-file-width="731" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man%2C_1955.jpg/220px-Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man%2C_1955.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man%2C_1955.jpg/330px-Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man%2C_1955.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man%2C_1955.jpg/440px-Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man%2C_1955.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Body_of_Maroon_child_brought_before_medicine_man,_1955.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Body of Ndyuka <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" title="Maroon (people)">Maroon</a> child brought before <a href="/wiki/Medicine_man" title="Medicine man">medicine man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname_River" title="Suriname River">Suriname River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, South America</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urarina" title="Urarina">Urarina</a> of the Peruvian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazonia" title="Amazonia">Amazonia</a> have an elaborate cosmological system predicated on the <a href="/wiki/Ritual" title="Ritual">ritual</a> consumption of <a href="/wiki/Ayahuasca" title="Ayahuasca">ayahuasca</a>, which is a key feature of their society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upf.com_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-upf.com-192">[192]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Santo_Daime" title="Santo Daime">Santo Daime</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uni%C3%A3o_do_Vegetal" title="União do Vegetal">União do Vegetal</a> ( abbreviated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UDV" title="UDV">UDV</a>) are syncretic religions with which use an <a href="/wiki/Entheogen" title="Entheogen">entheogen</a> called ayahuasca in an attempt to connect with the spirit realm and receive divine guidance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peru_57-4"><a href="#cite_note-Peru-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Amazonia">Amazonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Amazonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3504" data-file-width="2336" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg/220px-Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg/330px-Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg/440px-Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chaman_amazonie_5_06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shaman from the shuara culture in <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazonian_forest" title="Amazonian forest">Amazonian forest</a>, June 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1790" data-file-width="1212" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg/220px-Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg/330px-Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg/440px-Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Urarina_shaman_B_Dean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urarina" title="Urarina">Urarina</a> shaman, 1988</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Peruvian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a> and north coastal regions of the country, the healers are known as <a href="/wiki/Curandero" title="Curandero">curanderos</a>. <i>Ayahuasqueros</i> are Peruvians who specialize in the use of <a href="/wiki/Ayahuasca" title="Ayahuasca">ayahuasca</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-upf.com_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-upf.com-192">[192]</a></sup> <i>Ayahuasqueros</i> have become popular among Western spiritual seekers, who claim that the <i>ayauasqueros</i> and their ayahuasca brews have cured them of everything from depression to addiction to cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peru_57-5"><a href="#cite_note-Peru-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to <i>curanderos</i> use of ayahuasca and their ritualized ingestion of <a href="/wiki/Mescaline" title="Mescaline">mescaline</a>-bearing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Pedro_cactus" title="San Pedro cactus">San Pedro cactuses</a> (Trichocereus pachanoi) for the <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">divination</a> and diagnosis of <a href="/wiki/Maleficium_(sorcery)" title="Maleficium (sorcery)">sorcery</a>, north-coastal shamans are famous throughout the region for their intricately complex and symbolically dense healing <a href="/wiki/Altar" title="Altar">altars</a> called mesas (tables).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Sharon (1993) has argued that the mesas symbolize the dualistic ideology underpinning the practice and experience of north-coastal shamanism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> For Sharon, the mesas are the, "physical embodiment of the supernatural opposition between benevolent and malevolent energies" (Dean 1998: 61).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In several tribes living in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>, the spiritual leaders also act as managers of scarce ecological resources<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eco_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-eco-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecopia_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-ecopia-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coop_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-coop-92">[92]</a></sup> The rich symbolism in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tukano_people" title="Tukano people">Tukano</a> culture has been documented in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_work" title="Field work">field works</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eco_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-eco-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hug-FrMilkRiv_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hug-FrMilkRiv-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hug-PalmPlei_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hug-PalmPlei-196">[196]</a></sup> even in the last decades of the 20th century.</p>
<p>The <i>yaskomo</i> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wai-Wai_people" title="Wai-Wai people">Waiwai</a> is believed to be able to perform a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_travel" title="Soul travel">soul flight</a>. The soul flight can serve several functions:</p>
<ul>
<li>healing</li>
<li>flying to the sky to consult cosmological beings (the moon or the brother of the moon) to get a name for a newborn baby</li>
<li>flying to the cave of <i>peccaries' mountains</i> to ask the <i>father of peccaries</i> for abundance of game</li>
<li>flying deep down in a river, to achieve the help of other beings.</li>
</ul>
<p>Thus, a yaskomo is believed to be able to reach sky, earth, and water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yaskomo_soul_flight_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-yaskomo_soul_flight-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Mapuche">Mapuche</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Mapuche">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Among the <a href="/wiki/Mapuche" title="Mapuche">Mapuche</a> people of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machi_(Shaman)" title="Machi (Shaman)">Machi</a></i> is usually a woman who serves the community by performing ceremonies to cure diseases, ward off evil, influence the weather and harvest, and by practicing other forms of healing such as herbalism.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Aymara">Aymara</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Aymara">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymara</a> people of South America the <a href="/wiki/Yatiri" title="Yatiri">Yatiri</a> is a healer who heals the body and the soul, they serve the community and do the rituals for <a href="/wiki/Pachamama" title="Pachamama">Pachamama</a>. The Aymara and quechua nosology is based on traditional medical concepts still used by andean healers and shaman <i>altomisayok</i> , such as <i>oraken catjata</i> in aymara,<i>hallpa hapisqan</i>in quechua which means seized by the earth, or jintilin catjata <i>in aymara, machuq hapisqan</i> seized by the tomb,<i>airi</i> in aymara, <i>wayra hapisqan</i>seized by the wind, <i>puquio onccoy</i> the disease of the source, <i>rayu puritan catjata</i> in aymara, illa hapisqan in quechua, the disease secondary to a thunderbolt strike, among other diseases. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=(M%C3%A9decins_et_Chamanes_des_Andes,_Francois_Luis-Blanc,_Editions_l%27Harmattan,_Paris,_1995,_ISBN_2-7384-3140-2)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="(Médecins et Chamanes des Andes, Francois Luis-Blanc, Editions l'Harmattan, Paris, 1995, ISBN 2-7384-3140-2) (page does not exist)">(Médecins et Chamanes des Andes, Francois Luis-Blanc, Editions l'Harmattan, Paris, 1995, ISBN 2-7384-3140-2)</a> Part of the healing power attributed to shamanic practices depends of the use of plant alkaloids taken during the therapeutic sessions <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=(Trance_and_Shamanic_Cure_on_the_South_American_Continent:_Psychopharmalogical_and_Neurobiological_Interpretations,_Anthropology_of_Consciousness,_Vol.21,_Issue_1,_pp._83-105,ISSN_1053-4202,_2010)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="(Trance and Shamanic Cure on the South American Continent: Psychopharmalogical and Neurobiological Interpretations, Anthropology of Consciousness, Vol.21, Issue 1, pp. 83-105,ISSN 1053-4202, 2010) (page does not exist)">(Trance and Shamanic Cure on the South American Continent: Psychopharmalogical and Neurobiological Interpretations, Anthropology of Consciousness, Vol.21, Issue 1, pp. 83-105,ISSN 1053-4202, 2010)</a>.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuegians">Fuegians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Fuegians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet"><img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">rendering support</a>, you may see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Fuegians" title="Fuegians">Fuegians</a> (the indigenous peoples of <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>) were all <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> they did not share a common culture. The material culture was not homogenous, either: the big island and the archipelago made two different adaptations possible. Some of the cultures were coast-dwelling, others were land-oriented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ser-Hun_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ser-Hun-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ExtAnc_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-ExtAnc-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selk%27nam" title="Selk'nam">Selk'nam</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A1mana" title="Yámana">Yámana</a> had persons filling in shaman-like roles. The Selk'nams believed their <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xon/</span>s to have supernatural capabilities, e.g. to control weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The figure of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xon/</span> appeared in myths, too.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The Yámana <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jekamuʃ/</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> corresponds to the Selknam <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xon/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Umbarra" title="Umbarra">Umbarra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunggal_panaluan" title="Tunggal panaluan">Tunggal panaluan</a></div>
<p>On the island of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, indigenous tribes believe that illness and calamity are caused by dark spirits, or <i>masalai</i>, which cling to a person's body and <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poison</a> them. Shamans are summoned in order to purge the unwholesome spirits from a person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FourCorners_Amazon_entry_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FourCorners_Amazon_entry-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FourCornersWeb_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FourCornersWeb-207">[207]</a></sup> Shamans also perform <a href="/wiki/Rainmaking" title="Rainmaking">rainmaking</a> ceremonies and can allegedly improve a hunter's ability to catch animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MakingRain_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-MakingRain-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia various aboriginal groups refer to their shamans as "clever men" and "clever women" also as <i>kadji</i>. These aboriginal shamans use <i><a href="/wiki/Maban" title="Maban">maban</a></i> or <i>mabain</i>, the material that is believed to give them their purported magical powers. Besides healing, contact with spiritual beings, involvement in initiation and other secret ceremonies, they are also enforcers of tribal laws, keepers of special knowledge and may "<a href="/wiki/Curse" title="Curse">hex</a>" to death one who breaks a social taboo by singing a song only known to the "clever men".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" title="African traditional religion">African traditional religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Traditional_healers_of_South_Africa" title="Traditional healers of South Africa">Traditional healers of South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">Witch doctor</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangoma" title="Sangoma">Sangoma</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg/220px-Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg/330px-Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg/440px-Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sangoma_performing_a_Baptism.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_Healers_of_South_Africa" title="Traditional Healers of South Africa">Sangoma/Inyanga</a> performing a traditional baptism on a baby in order to protect the spirit of the baby, Johannesburg, South Africa</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dogon_people" title="Dogon people">Dogon</a> sorcerers (both male and female) communicate with a spirit named Amma, who advises them on healing and divination practices.</p>
<p>The classical meaning of shaman as a person who, after recovering from a mental illness (or insanity) takes up the professional calling of socially recognized religious practitioner, is exemplified among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sisala" title="Sisala">Sisala</a> (of northern Gold Coast) : "the fairies "seized" him and made him insane for several months. Eventually, though, he learned to control their power, which he now uses to divine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sangoma" title="Sangoma">sangoma</a></i>, as employed in <a href="/wiki/Zulu_people" title="Zulu people">Zulu</a> and congeneric languages, is effectively equivalent to shaman. Sangomas are highly revered and respected in their society, where illness is thought to be caused by <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> pollution (contact with impure objects or occurrences), bad spirits, or the ancestors themselves,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> either malevolently, or through neglect if they are not respected, or to show an individual her calling to become a sangoma (<i>thwasa</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> For harmony between the living and the dead, vital for a trouble-free life, the ancestors must be shown respect through ritual and animal sacrifice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inyanga" title="Inyanga">inyanga</a></i> also employed by the <a href="/wiki/Nguni_people" title="Nguni people">Nguni</a> cultures is equivalent to 'herbalist' as used by the Zulu people and a variation used by the <a href="/wiki/Shona_people" title="Shona people">Karanga</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> among whom remedies (locally known as <a href="/wiki/Muti" title="Muti">muti</a>) for ailments are discovered by the inyanga being informed in a dream, of the herb able to effect the cure and also of where that herb is to be found. The majority of the herbal knowledge base is passed down from one <i>inyanga</i> to the next, often within a particular family circle in any one village.</p>
<p>Shamanism is known among the Nuba of Kordofan in Sudan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_Western_shamanism">Contemporary Western shamanism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Contemporary Western shamanism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Neoshamanism" title="Neoshamanism">Neoshamanism</a></div>
<p>There is an endeavor in some contemporary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occultism" title="Occultism">occult</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esotericism" title="Esotericism">esoteric</a> circles to reinvent shamanism in a modern form, often drawing from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Core_shamanism" title="Core shamanism">core shamanism</a>—a set of beliefs and practices synthesized by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Harner" title="Michael Harner">Michael Harner</a>—centered on the use of ritual drumming and dance, and Harner's interpretations of various indigenous religions. Harner has faced criticism for taking pieces of diverse religions out of their cultural contexts and synthesising a set of universal shamanic techniques. Some neoshamans focus on the ritual use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entheogens" title="Entheogens">entheogens</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and also embrace the philosophies of <a href="/wiki/Chaos_magic" title="Chaos magic">chaos magic</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> while others (such as <a href="/wiki/Jan_Fries" title="Jan Fries">Jan Fries</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> have created their own forms of shamanism.</p>
<p>European-based neoshamanic traditions are focused upon the researched or imagined traditions of ancient Europe, where many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mystical" title="Mystical">mystical</a> practices and belief systems were suppressed by the Christian church. Some of these practitioners express a desire to practice a system that is based upon their own ancestral traditions. Some anthropologists and practitioners have discussed the impact of such neoshamanism as "giving extra pay" (Harvey, 1997 and elsewhere) to indigenous American traditions, particularly as many pagan or heathen shamanic practitioners do not call themselves shamans, but instead use specific names derived from the European traditions—they work within such as <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lva" title="Völva">völva</a></i> or <i>seidkona</i> (<a href="/wiki/Sei%C3%B0r" title="Seiðr">seid-woman</a>) of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sagas" title="Sagas">sagas</a> (see Blain 2002, Wallis 2003).</p>
<p>Many spiritual seekers travel to Peru to work with <i>ayahuasqueros</i>, shamans who engage in the ritual use of <a href="/wiki/Ayahuasca" title="Ayahuasca">ayahuasca</a>, a psychedelic tea which has been documented to cure everything from depression to addiction. When taking ayahuasca, participants frequently report meeting spirits, and receiving divine revelations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peru_57-6"><a href="#cite_note-Peru-57">[57]</a></sup> Shamanistic techniques have also been used in New Age therapies which use enactment and association with other realities as an intervention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_the_term">Criticism of the term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shamanism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Criticism of the term">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Medicine_man" title="Medicine man">medicine man</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shaman_tableau.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1342" data-file-width="1705" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Shaman_tableau.png/220px-Shaman_tableau.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Shaman_tableau.png/330px-Shaman_tableau.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Shaman_tableau.png/440px-Shaman_tableau.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shaman_tableau.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A tableau presenting figures of various cultures filling in mediator-like roles, often being termed as "shaman" in the literature. The tableau presents the diversity of this concept.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The anthropologist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alice_Kehoe" title="Alice Kehoe">Alice Kehoe</a> criticizes the term "shaman" in her book <i>Shamans and Religion: An Anthropological Exploration in Critical Thinking</i>. Part of this criticism involves the notion of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_appropriation" title="Cultural appropriation">cultural appropriation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waveland_Press_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Waveland_Press-7">[7]</a></sup> This includes criticism of <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> and modern Western forms of shamanism, which, according to Kehoe, misrepresent or dilute indigenous practices. Alice Kehoe also believes that the term reinforces racist ideas such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noble_Savage" title="Noble Savage">Noble Savage</a>.</p>
<p>Kehoe is highly critical of <a href="/wiki/Mircea_Eliade" title="Mircea Eliade">Mircea Eliade</a>'s work on shamanism as an invention synthesized from various sources unsupported by more direct research. To Kehoe, citing that ritualistic practices (most notably drumming, trance, chanting, entheogens and hallucinogens, spirit communication and healing) as being definitive of shamanism is poor practice. Such citations ignore the fact that those practices exist outside of what is defined as shamanism and play similar roles even in non-shamanic cultures (such as the role of chanting in <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Christian" title="Judeo-Christian">Judeo-Christian</a> and Islamic rituals) and that in their expression are unique to each culture that uses them. Such practices cannot be generalized easily, accurately, or usefully into a global religion of shamanism. Because of this, Kehoe is also highly critical of the hypothesis that shamanism is an ancient, unchanged, and surviving religion from the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waveland_Press_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Waveland_Press-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anthropologist <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mih%C3%A1ly_Hopp%C3%A1l&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mihály Hoppál (page does not exist)">Mihály Hoppál</a> also discusses whether the term "shamanism" is appropriate. He notes that for many readers, "-ism" implies a particular dogma, like Buddhism or Judaism. He recommends using the term "shamanhood"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summer_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-summer-220">[220]</a></sup> or "shamanship"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> (a term used in old Russian and German <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">ethnographic</a> reports at the beginning of the 20th century) for stressing the diversity and the specific features of the discussed cultures. He believes that this places more stress on the local variations<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cogmap_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-cogmap-15">[15]</a></sup> and emphasizes that shamanism is not a religion of sacred <a href="/wiki/Dogma" title="Dogma">dogmas</a>, but linked to the everyday life in a practical way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Following similar thoughts, he also conjectures a contemporary paradigm shift.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-summer_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-summer-220">[220]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Piers_Vitebsky" title="Piers Vitebsky">Piers Vitebsky</a> also mentions that, despite really astonishing similarities, there is no unity in shamanism. The various, fragmented shamanistic practices and beliefs coexist with other beliefs everywhere. There is no record of pure shamanistic societies (although, as for the past, their existence is not impossible).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-Wernitznig2-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Wernitznig2_8-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Wernitznig, Dagmar, <i>Europe's Indians, Indians in Europe: European Perceptions and Appropriations of Native American Cultures from Pocahontas to the Present</i>. University Press of America, 2007: p.132. "What happens further in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plastic_Shaman" title="Plastic Shaman">Plastic Shaman</a>'s [fictitious] story is highly irritating from a perspective of cultural hegemony. The Injun elder does not only willingly share their spirituality with the white intruder but, in fact, must come to the conclusion that this intruder is as good an Indian as they are themselves. Regarding Indian spirituality, the Plastic Shaman even out-Indians the actual ones. The messianic element, which Plastic Shamanism financially draws on, is installed in the Yoda-like elder themselves. They are the ones – while melodramatically parting from their spiritual offshoot – who urge the Plastic Shaman to share their gift with the rest of the world. Thus Plastic Shamans wipe their hands clean of any megalomaniac or missionizing undertones. Licensed by the authority of an Indian elder, they now have every right to spread their wisdom, and if they make (quite more than) a buck with it, then so be it.—The neocolonial ideology attached to this scenario leaves less room for cynicism."</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-171"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-171">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Рубцова 1954: 203, 209</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-172"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-172">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Both death of a person and successfully hunted game require that cutting, sewing etc. be tabooed, so that the invisible soul does not get hurt accidentally (Kleivan &amp; Sonne, pp. 18–21). In Greenland, the transgression of death tabu could turn the soul of the dead into a <i>tupilak</i>, a restless ghost which scared game away (Kleivan &amp; Sonne 1985, p. 23). Animals fled from hunter in case of taboo breaches, e.g. birth taboo, death taboo (Kleivan &amp; Sonne, pp. 12–13)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-complink-173"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-complink_173-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.uaf.edu/anlc/yupik_inuit.html" rel="nofollow">Lawrence Kaplan: Comparative Yupik and Inuit</a> (found on the site of <a class="external text" href="http://www.uaf.edu/anlc/index.html" rel="nofollow">Alaska Native Language Center</a>)</span></li>

<tr>
<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Major historic treatises</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Formicarius" title="Formicarius">Formicarius</a></i> (1475)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Summis_desiderantes_affectibus" title="Summis desiderantes affectibus">Summis desiderantes affectibus</a></i> (1484)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Malleus_Maleficarum" title="Malleus Maleficarum">Malleus Maleficarum</a></i> (1487)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Discoverie_of_Witchcraft" title="The Discoverie of Witchcraft">The Discoverie of Witchcraft</a></i> (1584)</li>

<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Discovery_of_Witches" title="The Discovery of Witches">The Discovery of Witches</a></i> (1647)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Trait%C3%A9_sur_les_apparitions_des_esprits_et_sur_les_vampires_ou_les_revenans_de_Hongrie,_de_Moravie,_%26c." title="Traité sur les apparitions des esprits et sur les vampires ou les revenans de Hongrie, de Moravie, &amp;c.">Traité sur les apparitions des esprits et sur les vampires ou les revenans de Hongrie, de Moravie, &amp;c.</a></i> (1751)</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
